The flawed Harvard study-Seacoast Online

Source: https://www.seacoastonline.com/story/opinion/columns/2026/01/10/nh-urged-to-probe-health-impacts-near-seabrook-nuclear-plant-beriont/88093976007/

NH urged to probe health impacts near Seabrook nuclear plant: Beriont

Published: Jan. 10, 2026, 5:02 a.m. ET By: Carleigh Beriont

TL;DR

• A Harvard study found that living closer to nuclear power plants is associated with higher cancer rates, including data from New Hampshire's Seabrook Station • The author calls for New Hampshire and UNH to conduct an independent health assessment of cancer risks near Seabrook Station • Drawing from experience in the Marshall Islands, the author warns about long-term health consequences of nuclear policy decisions and criticizes the Trump administration's efforts to weaken nuclear safety oversight

Personal Experience with Nuclear Impact

From 2010 to 2013, I lived in the Marshall Islands. And between 2015 and 2020, I returned to conduct research. I worked with communities still suffering from the impact of policy decisions made decades ago and thousands of miles away by people they'd never met or even seen. This is part of the legacy of U.S. nuclear power.

From 1946 to 1958, the U.S. tested 67 nuclear weapons in the Marshall Islands. Generations later, Marshallese people are continuing to deal with the aftermath, including cancer and struggles with pregnancy complicated by radiation-related birth defects. Living in the Marshall Islands offers a lesson that "half-life" is more than a scientific term; it is a metaphor for the ways reckless policymakers can rob generations of the right to a full and vibrant life.

I didn't have to travel thousands of miles to learn this lesson. Activists who waded into the marshes of Seabrook and Hampton before I was born worried about the risks posed by nuclear radiation right here on the Seacoast.

Harvard Study Findings

A recent study led by researchers at the Harvard T.H Chan School of Public Health found that living closer to a nuclear power plant is associated with higher cancer rates, with risk increasing with age and decreasing the farther from these plants people live. The study examined data from seven nuclear power plants located within 120km of Massachusetts zip codes, including Seabrook Station in New Hampshire.

As the Trump administration rushes to eliminate regulation and oversight of the nuclear industry and extract personal profit by inking a $6 billion deal between his social media platform and a company that is attempting to develop nuclear fusion technology, these findings underscore a critical need to examine public health risks alongside energy policy decisions.

Calls for Action

That's why I'm calling on the state of New Hampshire and the University of New Hampshire to promptly review this study and conduct an independent assessment of cancer risks and other potential health impacts associated with the Seabrook Station. I am also calling on the Trump administration to halt efforts to weaken nuclear safety oversight and ensure that health risk monitoring keeps pace with plant operations and scientific evidence. Finally, I call on members of Congress to investigate financial ties between the president and members of his administration and the nuclear power industry to ensure that public servants don't put personal profit over public health.

When the government fails to proactively protect public health, families are left to carry the uncertainty. That's why I'm running for Congress. I'm a mom and a teacher, and I believe that children in New Hampshire's Seacoast deserve to grow up with the confidence that their air, water, and environment are being safeguarded based on science, not untested assumptions or empty assurances.

A Call for Transparency

Granite Staters understand this. We have a tradition of looking out for one another and valuing transparency. We can and should insist on efficient energy policy and strong health protections at the same time. If there is a necessary trade-off to be made between public health and climate-friendly energy policy, then it's a choice we should weigh with all the facts in hand, and it's a decision we all should have a say in making.

Carleigh Beriont is a historian who researches the history of U.S. Nuclear Policy in the Pacific. She teaches about the intersection of religion, politics, and public policy at the Harvard Kennedy School. A Hampton resident, she is a candidate for Congress in New Hampshire's 1st District.

AI Analysis

This opinion piece effectively combines personal experience with scientific evidence to make a compelling case for nuclear safety oversight. Beriont's background working with Marshall Islands communities affected by nuclear testing provides powerful context for understanding long-term health consequences. Her call for independent health assessments near Seabrook Station is timely given the Harvard study's findings, though the piece would benefit from more specific details about the study's methodology and statistical significance. The political criticisms of the Trump administration, while relevant to nuclear policy, may overshadow the core public health message for some readers.

📅Upcoming nuclear events-12th International Conference on Isotopes (12ICI)

Source: https://nam12.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Femail.news.ans.org%2Fc%2FeJyMkc1q3TAQhZ_G3oS5SKPR38KLQvEyr1DkmfGNwMjBUmPapy8JZN_1ORzOxycLRlbvZl1sDDGgRZ9nlTrq2X5VWTJGUpYIJYkBCnuAYgLBLlg2Ln73lOa3ZUuZk0c2FJN4I8lFHzCgkcziEs51QYPBWOOt82Tzw2T2GyWbVPYi6CYyTe_-KK0_zus5H8vbGO99cj8mXCdc7_t-XJ0_swlX_dA2-oSr6Cj1mHBNaL2ZcLU43qC2oVcrnxDlAD7brpc2Vjgb1H6O8107WKxc5_N6llb_lm9gNhE3Swm8wwAUpEDmSBAMWV-s5MhpvpbjqfWp10Tm-3DXJl8D2ZniNEKJmoCQEDbyDBYd2h33IhvPXa-q_atuN_LWG0CjDJT3DTYyGVCEUEpitGkey-tvPrRcL69695efpR5_5vF_cj4W_BcAAP__LA6Q1g&data=05%7C02%7Clgeiger%40ans.org%7C59416ca26b0d4e75f61c08de4c61ed24%7C167ee8c474f046ce9d341192bc28f12d%7C0%7C0%7C639032180681720325%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%3D%3D%7C0%7C%7C%7C&sdata=OcUy6Eg5xU%2Bnt05y1N7fzAYPDYy4vIIx7RkDi%2B2zowo%3D&reserved=0

12th International Conference on Isotopes - 12ICI

February 15-19, 2026

TL;DR

  • The 12th International Conference on Isotopes (12ICI) will take place in Florence, Italy from February 15-19, 2026, bringing together scientists and professionals from multiple disciplines
  • The conference covers isotope production, radiopharmaceuticals, nuclear medicine, environmental applications, and policy aspects across scientific, medical, and industrial fields
  • Features include 4 days of scientific sessions, plenary lectures, poster presentations, young scientist sessions, industrial exhibitions, and networking events in historic Florence

Introduction

The 12th International Conference on Isotopes (12ICI) will be held in Florence, Italy, from 15 to 19 February 2026.

This international event provides a multidisciplinary platform for scientists, professionals, and stakeholders to share knowledge on the production, applications, and regulation of isotopes across scientific, medical, industrial, and environmental fields.

Conference Themes and Topics

  • Isotope production and separation
  • Radiopharmaceuticals and nuclear medicine
  • Environmental and geological applications
  • Energy, decommissioning, and nuclear safeguards
  • Policy, economics, and global impact of isotope use

Aims and Objectives

12ICI aims to foster interdisciplinary dialogue, promote innovation, and strengthen collaboration across academia, research institutions, regulatory bodies, and industry.

Target Audience

Scientists, medical physicists, chemists, radiochemists, nuclear engineers, health professionals, environmental researchers, policy makers, and representatives from industry.

Programme Structure

  • 4 days of scientific sessions
  • Plenary lectures, parallel tracks, and poster presentations
  • Young Scientists Session and Marie Curie Session
  • Industrial exhibition and technical workshops

Registration and Submissions

Call for papers and abstract submission: Abstract submissions are open until October 31, 2025 via the conference website: https://agenda.infn.it/event/41820 Registration: Registration is open with discounted fees for students and early-career researchers. Information available at: https://agenda.infn.it/event/41820/page/9652-information-on-registrations

Social Programme

Networking events, welcome reception, guided technical tours, and a gala dinner in a historical venue in Florence.

Venue

Palazzo dei Congressi Piazza Ardua, 1 Florence, 50123, Italy

• The ANS Student Conference 2026 will be held at Texas A&M University in College Station, TX, from April 16-18, 2026, with the theme "Don't Mess with Nuclear: Leading the Way" • The call for papers is now open for students to submit summaries or abstracts on new and significant work in the nuclear field, including internship projects, senior design projects, and research • Sponsorship opportunities are available with various packages that include recognition on the conference website and in promotional materials

See you in Texas!

The ANS student section at Texas A&M University is excited to welcome students from across the world to the heart of Aggieland for the ANS Student Conference 2026.

Conference Theme

Rooted in the bold spirit of Texas, "Don't Mess with Nuclear" embodies both the resilience and responsibility that define the pursuit of nuclear technology. Drawing inspiration from the iconic "Don't Mess with Texas" slogan, this theme celebrates a culture of pride, professionalism, and technical excellence within nuclear science and engineering.

In recent years, our world has endured extraordinary challenges, from global pandemics to pressing energy crises. Through it all, nuclear technology has stood as a steadfast symbol of stability, innovation, and progress. This theme calls on students to mirror that same strength, rising to meet challenges with resolve and driving boldly toward a brighter, more sustainable future.

  • Senior design projects

📅Upcoming nuclear events-Digital Tools for Power Uprates: Using DVR and PEPSE to Enhance MUR and Performance Studies

Source: https://www.ans.org/webinars/view-cw2026/

Digital Tools for Power Uprates: Using DVR and PEPSE to Enhance MUR and Performance Studies

January 27, 2026 | 1:00–2:00PM (2:00–3:00PM EST)

TL;DR

• This ANS and Curtiss-Wright webinar explores digital technologies transforming nuclear power uprate projects, specifically focusing on Data Validation & Reconciliation (DVR) technology and PEPSE plant modeling software • The session will demonstrate how DVR, which is approved for Measurement Uncertainty Recapture (MUR) uprates, improves data accuracy and supports uprate justification with practical case examples • Industry experts will share best practices for using PEPSE software to perform power uprate studies and assess plant performance impacts in real-world applications

Event Details

Available to All Users

The webinar is scheduled for January 27, 2026, from 1:00–2:00PM (2:00–3:00PM EST). Registration and calendar integration are available through the ANS website.

Overview

Join ANS and Curtiss-Wright for a Supplier Showcase webinar featuring a deep dive into the digital technologies transforming power uprate projects. We'll highlight Data Validation & Reconciliation (DVR)—a technology approved for MUR uprates—and demonstrate how it improves data accuracy and supports uprate justification. We'll also explore best practices for using PEPSE, the industry-standard plant modeling and simulation software, to perform power uprate studies and assess plant performance impacts. This webinar will provide practical insights, case-style examples, and actionable approaches for applying these tools in real uprate projects.

Featured Speakers

Derek Horn Sr. Manager of Business Development, Curtiss-Wright

Derek brings experience from a variety of power industries, including nuclear energy. He has extensive experience in thermal performance, with a strong focus on areas such as online performance monitoring, data validation and reconciliation (DVR), PEPSE modeling, cycle isolation, and life cycle management. In addition to his technical background, he also has valuable project management experience across these domains. Derek has also been actively involved with numerous regulatory required engineering programs such Inservice Testing and Inservice Inspection and continues to be an active member of two ASME international working groups (Sec. XI and O&M). Fun fact—Derek is trilingual! He's fluent in Mandarin Chinese, Spanish, and English.

Greg Alder Director of Plant Optimization, Curtiss-Wright

Greg is an experienced professional in the field of engineering and plant optimization, currently serving as the Manager of Plant Optimization at Curtiss-Wright since October 2013. Prior to this role, Greg held the position of Senior Consultant at True North Consulting from January 2008 to October 2013 and also served as a Senior Consultant and Business Development Manager at Scientech for two decades, from January 1988 to January 2008. Greg Alder holds a Bachelor of Science degree in Mechanical Engineering from the University of Idaho, obtained between 1985 and 1987, and an Associate's degree in Engineering from Brigham Young University - Idaho, completed from 1983 to 1985.

Sponsorship

This webinar is sponsored by Curtiss-Wright.

AI Analysis

This webinar represents an important intersection of digital transformation and nuclear power optimization, focusing on technologies that can help existing nuclear plants increase their output safely and efficiently. The combination of DVR and PEPSE tools addresses critical needs in the nuclear industry for accurate data analysis and comprehensive plant modeling during uprate projects. The speakers bring decades of combined experience in thermal performance and plant optimization, suggesting attendees will receive practical, industry-tested insights. Given the nuclear industry's focus on extending plant life and maximizing capacity, this technical presentation could provide valuable guidance for utilities considering power uprate projects. The regulatory approval of DVR for MUR uprates particularly highlights the practical applicability of these digital tools in real-world nuclear operations.

2026 North American Radiation Safety & Technology Exhibition Symposium

Date: January 13-15, 2026

TL;DR

• The 2026 North American Radiation Safety & Technology Exhibition Symposium will be held January 13-15, 2026, at the Sheraton Sand Key in Clearwater Beach, Florida, focusing on "Change Management in Radiation Protection Programs at NPPs" • The symposium serves as the premier regulatory/RPM meeting featuring presentations from US NRC commissioners, radiation protection managers, and industry experts sharing operational experience and lessons learned • The event includes three days of programming covering ALARA challenges, regulatory updates, technology innovations, and regional RPM meetings for radiation protection professionals from the US, Canada, and Mexico

Event Overview

The 2026 North American Radiation Safety & Technology Exhibition Symposium will be held January 13-15, 2026 at the Sheraton Sand Key, Florida (1160 Gulf Blvd, Clearwater Beach, FL 33767). This premier regulatory/RPM meeting continues the tradition established in 1997 by the North American Technical Center (NATC).

Theme: Change Management in Radiation Protection Programs at NPPs

The symposium objective is to provide presentations on recent radiation protection operational experience, good practices, and lessons learned, especially focusing on current change management initiatives to promote safe and efficient nuclear power operations.

Background

Since 1992, the Grainger College of Engineering at the University of Illinois has hosted the North American Technical Center for the Information System on Occupational Exposure (ISOE) OECD NEA/IAEA. NATC comprises Canadian, Mexican, and USA nuclear utilities and regulatory authorities. The NATC Board founded the ISOE ALARA symposium in 1997, with annual symposia held since 1999.

Schedule

Tuesday, January 13, 2026 (8 am – 5 pm EST)

Day 1: Including plenary speakers (U.S. NRC Commission Chair invited), 2025 World Class Performance ALARA Award, and RPM presentations on outage operational experience lessons learned.

Wednesday, January 14, 2026 (8 am – 5 pm EST)

Day 2: Morning sessions on radiation protection ALARA challenges and successes. Afternoon session includes U.S. NRC regulatory presentations on observations from ALARA inspection programs, regulation revisions, and NRC findings from 2023-2025. Canadian RP inspection program feedback will also be included.

Thursday, January 15, 2026 (8 am – 12 pm EST)

Day 3: Industry speakers from NEI, EPRI, INPO, and RPM operational radiological events/lessons learned.

Thursday, January 15, 2026 (1 pm – 5 pm EST)

Region III RPM Meeting: Observations from NRC Branch Chief and RP Inspectors regarding control of RP programs.

Symposium Highlights

The annual symposium has grown steadily since 1997, with utility radiation protection managers attending from the U.S., Canada, and Mexico. The 2026 symposium will focus on:

  • 2025 refueling outage experience
  • CANDU refurbishments
  • Mentoring on health physics innovative technology
  • Latest approaches in work management and dose control
  • Pixelated 3D CZT technology
  • Remote monitoring and AI applications
  • Source term reduction
  • Personnel dosimetry QA lessons learned

Call for Papers

Authors interested in presenting are requested to send paper titles and abstracts to:

  • Amy Keep: almoeller88@gmail.com
  • David W. Miller: dmiller@illinois.edu

Registration and Hotel Information

Symposium Registration: Available through event registration portal
>
Hotel Reservations: Group rates available at Sheraton Sand Key for both general attendees and government rate reservations

Contact Information

Amy Keep NATC Executive Administrator/Event Coordinator Email: almoeller88@gmail.com Phone: 269-930-0753 David W. Miller NATC Regional Director, NPRE, University of Illinois Email: dmiller@illinois.edu Phone: 217-855-3238

Nuclear Fuels and Materials

Date: May 31–June 3, 2026 Location: Denver, CO | Sheraton Denver

TL;DR

• The Nuclear Fuels and Materials (NFM) 2026 conference will focus on accelerating advanced nuclear fuel and materials development to meet growing energy demands • The event addresses the critical gap between nuclear energy needs and deployment, emphasizing the role of nuclear power in industrial expansion and data center growth • The conference aims to support the ambitious goal of quadrupling nuclear power generation in the United States by 2050

---

Event Details

Sponsored by: Materials Science & Technology Add to Calendar

Call for Papers Now Open

Across the world, nuclear power production stands at the threshold of a new era driven by rapid industrial expansion, electrification, and the growth of data centers. Nuclear energy offers scalable, 24/7, and domestically controlled energy source industry, manufacturing, and national security. However, there is a significant gap between need and deployment.

Accelerating the development, qualification, and deployment of advanced next generation nuclear fuels and materials is essential for the deployment of advanced nuclear to dramatically shorten the timeline for fuel innovation and qualification. This embedded topical meeting is focused on the materials and nuclear fuels research efforts that will enable the increased deployment of nuclear reactors to meet the energy imperative of quadrupling the generation of nuclear power in the United States by 2050.

SUBMIT AN ABSTRACT

Organizers

| Role | Name | |------|------| | General Chair: | Simon M. Pimblott (Idaho National Laboratory) | | Program Chair: | Jake Quincey (Kairos Power) |

The focus on materials science and fuel technology is particularly strategic, as these are often the longest lead-time components in nuclear reactor development. The collaboration between national laboratories and private industry, as evidenced by the organizers' affiliations, suggests a strong emphasis on bridging the gap between fundamental research and commercial application.

Technology of Fusion Energy (TOFE 2026)

May 31–June 3, 2026 | Denver, CO | Sheraton Denver

TL;DR

• TOFE 2026 will bring together global fusion scientists, engineers, and industry leaders to address the urgent need for developing a robust fusion energy supply chain as the industry moves toward commercial deployment • The conference will focus on fusion pilot plant design, materials development, manufacturing readiness, and supply chain resilience, with opportunities to tour regional facilities • The call for papers is now open, with accepted abstracts eligible for presentation and potential publication in a special issue of Fusion Science & Technology journal

---

Recent progress toward fusion pilot plants and the rapid growth of the commercial fusion sector have brought new urgency to developing a robust and scalable fusion energy supply chain. TOFE 2026 invites scientists, engineers, manufacturers, and industry leaders from around the world to explore how research, technology innovation, and industrial partnerships are converging to enable deployment-ready fusion systems.

A mix of invited and contributed talks will address topics including:

  • Fusion pilot plant design
  • Component and materials development
  • Enabling technologies
  • Manufacturing readiness and supply chain resilience

Attendees will also have opportunities to tour regional facilities that support fusion and advanced energy technologies. Denver, Colorado—a growing hub for high-technology manufacturing and energy innovation—will provide an inspiring setting for collaboration and discussion.

Call for Papers Now Open

Abstracts will be accepted as presentations based on technical merit, novelty of methods, and impact on the advancement of fusion energy. Presentations will be in the format of talks or posters. Space permitting, abstracts not selected for talks will be considered as posters. The final session topics and tracks will be finalized once all abstracts are received.

Authors of accepted, presented abstracts may submit a journal manuscript to the Fusion Science & Technology (FS&T) TOFE special issue after the meeting.

Organizers

  • General Chair: Brian Grierson (General Atomics)
  • Program Chair: Lane Carasik (Virginia Commonwealth University)

Conference Resources

  • Submit an Abstract
  • Add to Calendar
  • TOFE Abstract Template
  • TOFE 2026 Call for Papers

---

AI Analysis: TOFE 2026 represents a pivotal moment in fusion energy development, strategically positioned at the intersection of scientific advancement and commercial viability. The conference's emphasis on supply chain development and manufacturing readiness reflects the industry's maturation beyond pure research toward practical deployment considerations. Denver's selection as the venue is particularly strategic, leveraging the region's established high-tech manufacturing ecosystem and energy innovation infrastructure. The integration of facility tours with technical presentations demonstrates a comprehensive approach to knowledge transfer that bridges theoretical understanding with practical implementation. This conference timing aligns well with the current fusion industry momentum, where multiple companies are advancing toward demonstration plants and the need for industrial-scale solutions has never been more pressing.

Advanced Reactors Summit XIII & Technology Trailblazers Showcase

February 10-12, 2026 | Seattle, WA

TL;DR

• The Advanced Reactors Summit XIII is the flagship event for the advanced nuclear sector, bringing together technology developers, suppliers, utilities, investors, and policymakers to focus on deployment, cost reduction, and market opportunities.

• The summit features extensive sponsorship and exhibiting opportunities through the Technology Trailblazers Showcase, offering companies premier branding, thought-leadership roles, and access to decision-makers in the advanced nuclear space.

• The event will be held at the Seattle Marriott Waterfront with special hotel rates of $248 per night, featuring keynotes from DOE, NRC, and industry leaders, plus the prestigious Trailblazer Awards Reception.

Overview

Founded as the first conference devoted solely to advanced reactors, the Advanced Reactors Summit has grown into the sector's flagship event. Now in its thirteenth year, ARS XIII convenes the people who move projects from plan to plant. Past Summits have been hosted at world-class national labs (Argonne, Oak Ridge, Idaho), leading universities (UMass Lowell, Texas A&M, UC San Diego, University of Tennessee), a Virtual Summit, and innovation hubs (Charlotte, Houston, Salt Lake City). It's where the advanced nuclear community meets, plans, and gets business done.

Delivering Scale—The Global Rollout of Advanced Nuclear

ARS XIII brings together technology developers, supply-chain leaders, utilities and industrial offtakers, investors, and policymakers to tackle what matters most: cost, timelines, policy, and market opportunities. Expect candid, execution-focused sessions and practical pathways that align technology, supply chains, customers, capital, and policy—compressing schedules, lowering costs, and accelerating deployment.

Why attend: Unmatched access to decision-makers • Practical, deployment-focused sessions • Real opportunities for partnerships and deals Who's in the room: Reactor developers • Tier-1 suppliers & manufacturers • Utilities & industrial offtakers • Investors & lenders • Federal & state policymakers • Labs & regulators

Sponsorship & Exhibitor Opportunities

Showcase your brand and technology where advanced nuclear gets business done. The ARS XIII Technology Trailblazers Showcase is a curated forum to present, discuss, and display new and developing capabilities to a concentrated audience of decision-makers—reactor developers; Tier-1 suppliers and manufacturers; utilities and industrial offtakers; investors and lenders; national labs; regulators; and policymakers.

Timed with peak networking blocks, it maximizes qualified conversations, partnership building, and pipeline growth—so you leave with the relationships and insights to move initiatives forward.

Sponsor Benefits (snapshot):

  • Premier branding across plenaries, website, and onsite signage
  • Thought-leadership roles (moderation/remarks; subject to program fit)
  • Premium booth placement within the Showcase (for packages that include displays)
  • Exclusive lanyard co-branding (one sponsor)
  • Co-branded gift bags with approved inserts (one sponsor)
  • Sponsor-hosted reception opportunities
  • Advance registration list access (opt-in) for targeted outreach and meeting setting

Exhibitor Benefits (snapshot):

  • Exhibition space within the Technology Trailblazers Showcase
  • Premium booth placement along high-traffic areas
  • Logo placement on Summit materials & promotional collateral
  • Showcase times aligned to networking blocks to maximize engagement
Availability: Space is limited and prioritized by package level and commitment date. Reserve early to secure prime placement and visibility.

For more information on sponsorship and exhibiting please contact Caleb Ward at caleb.ward@usnic.org.

Advanced Reactors Summit XIII Sponsors & Exhibitors

The summit features multiple sponsorship tiers including Nuclear Titan & Summit Lead Sponsors, Trailblazer Award Reception Sponsors, ARS Welcoming Partners, Advanced Nuclear Champions, Trailblazer Exhibitors & Sponsors, Showcase Sponsors & Exhibitors, and Summit Supporters.

Source: https://nam12.safelinks.protection.outlook.com/?url=https%3A%2F%2Femail.news.ans.org%2Fc%2FeJyMkM1qHDEQhJ9mdDFapFbr76BDIOzRrxB6ultrwaIJM-MMydMHG3z3taqoKj5pkFljMNp8TjmBh1iNyjjHNn8NaRUyKku2VMRZTD1ZcgltF6CVKfaIxbw171S8AlXRWoEUeo2xcIgsmamoGQ0cJOdd9CGirzdXOa5YfFHpJBAWdFOv40bzuG37wzzb23n-PpbwY4H7Avfrum7vB43JH_aHMOapu-Vtdt11si5wN9v-oDn-0dd9dhlWj8XGAMliErKVM9rk0EfyUjMXs7fnQ8dD9wXd1_yhUz4LanAUNFvKWiwCgl0xsvUQwHfoJCubQ_ehx2fcrxh9dBacssXaV7uiqxZEEIQKgy_mbK_v_FTaX171Ol5-0nj-Nef3UP9p8D8AAP__unKBXg&data=05%7C02%7Clgeiger%40ans.org%7C59416ca26b0d4e75f61c08de4c61ed24%7C167ee8c474f046ce9d341192bc28f12d%7C0%7C0%7C639032180681672420%7CUnknown%7CTWFpbGZsb3d8eyJFbXB0eU1hcGkiOnRydWUsIlYiOiIwLjAuMDAwMCIsIlAiOiJXaW4zMiIsIkFOIjoiTWFpbCIsIldUIjoyfQ%3D%3D%7C0%7C%7C%7C&sdata=EpF05tqlmB39Ljm%2FJUNVwNJtMsNoz37IalLhtlZe5ws%3D&reserved=0

USA Supply Chain Winter Conference

TL;DR

  • USA Inc. hosts an annual Winter Conference each January bringing together utility members and supplier-partners for strategic planning, networking, and relationship building in the nuclear industry
  • The 2026 conference will be held January 20-22 in Palm Desert, California, featuring peer team meetings, supplier presentations, and hundreds of "speed-dating" sessions between utilities and suppliers
  • Past conferences have achieved excellent satisfaction rates, with 97% of 2025 attendees and 92% of 2024 attendees rating the conference as an "excellent" or "good" value for their investment

Conference Overview

Each year in January, the USA Supply Chain Management Team hosts a Winter Conference for its Members and Supplier-Partners. We seek a unique and beautiful venue where participants can get away from the day to day grind to focus on strategy, collaboration and plans for the coming year to maximize the mutual benefits available through Fleet participation and partnership. The Conference is unique in that in addition to outstanding informational presentations and networking opportunities, a significant part of the agenda is devoted to face-to-face meetings between utility members and suppliers. The intent of these break-out sessions is to provide focused time to discuss successes and opportunities to grow the relationships and maximize the benefits offered by USA Fleet Agreements with our world-class Supplier-Partners.

2026 Winter Conference

Palm Desert, California will be the scene for the 2026 USA Member & Supplier-Partner Winter Conference! Our 23rd annual winter conference will feature an outstanding schedule including meetings of the USA Innovations, Procurement Engineering, Site Representative and Supply Chain peer teams as well as private supplier "value-concept" presentations to key site stakeholders. No Winter Conference is complete without USA style "speed-dating", so we'll mix in a couple of hundred meetings between suppliers and utility representatives to discuss agreement status and ideas to grow relationships while enhancing the benefit enjoyed by all participants. We'll also have several engaging presentations during the General Session designed to inform and equip attendees on current industry issues as well as plans and goals for the new year.

Save the dates- January 20 – 22, 2026. Our 2026 USA Member & Supplier-Partner Winter Conference is sure to be a valuable and worthwhile experience, and we look forward to welcoming you to the beautiful desert southwest!

2025 Winter Conference

The weather was a bit chilly in Tucson as we gathered for our 22nd annual USA Member & Supplier-Partner Winter Conference, but the activity was hot inside as 200 attendees and guests gathered for networking, sharing of information, speed-dating and fun activities all designed to build relationships between USA members and Supplier-Partners. The week started with meetings of the USA Innovation, Procurement Engineering, Site Reps and Supply Chain teams, as well as numerous Value-Concept Presentations provided by our Supplier-Partners. Transitioning to the General Session Wednesday and Thursday, we enjoyed a great lineup of speakers, including new USA President & CEO Karen Fili (USA Update) and new USA Vice President – Nuclear Innovation & Industry Relations Clint Carter (Nuclear Innovation). Marc Tannenbaum, Sr. Technical Executive at EPRI returned to tell us about EPRI's activities and opportunities in 2025. Several other excellent presentations, including a panel discussion on implementation of the Inflation Reduction Act, as well as close to 300 "Speed Dating" meetings between suppliers and utility and USA staff kept everyone moving and engaged.

We strive to provide a great meeting for our guests and this year 97% of respondents saying the Conference was an "excellent" or "good" value for their investment of time and resources! Plans are in motion for 2026. We look forward to seeing you in Palm Desert, CA!

2024 Winter Conference

The 2024 USA Supply Chain Winter Conference was a grand success! Charleston, SC was the gathering place in late January as one of our largest groups ever celebrated the opportunity to come together in person around our common passion for the nuclear industry. The weather cooperated too, as attendees were able to thaw out in 60-70 degree temperatures all week! In addition to a General Session rich in content relevant to attendees, there were meetings of our Advanced Remote Monitoring, Site Representative and Supply Chain Management teams as well as roughly 400 individual sessions for supplier value-concept presentations and "speed-dating" meetings between USA member utilities and supplier-partners. Attendees completed a "5-Voices" assessment and received a complimentary training session by USA Supplier-Partner Dan Deeble of Lost Ball Consulting to better understand their communication styles and receive tips for recognizing and honoring the "voices" of everyone around the table. In addition to all the work, there were numerous opportunities for networking and catching up over a meal, and even checking out a few of the local attractions! Survey data from the Conference was excellent with 92% of respondents saying the Conference was an "excellent" or "good value" for their investment of time and resources. We'll be working hard to drive those numbers even higher in 2025 and hope to see you there!

AI Analysis

This conference appears to be a well-established and highly successful annual event that serves as a crucial networking and business development platform for the nuclear industry supply chain. The emphasis on "speed-dating" style meetings between utilities and suppliers is particularly innovative, creating structured opportunities for relationship building and business development. The consistently high satisfaction rates (92-97%) demonstrate the event's value proposition and effectiveness in meeting attendees' needs. The geographic rotation to attractive destinations like Charleston, Tucson, and Palm Desert also suggests thoughtful planning to encourage attendance while providing an appealing experience. The growth in attendance and number of individual meetings (from 300 in 2025 to 400 in 2024) indicates the conference's expanding influence and importance within the nuclear industry ecosystem.
